style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Total</div></th><td>3,903&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (1,507&#160;sq&#160;mi)&#32;(<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">not ranked</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left"><a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Demographics of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">Population</a></th></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Summer estimate</div></th><td>22</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Currency</th><td><a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands_pound" title="Falkland Islands pound">Falkland Islands pound</a> (£) (<a href="/wiki/ISO_4217" title="ISO 4217">FKP</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">Time zone</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/UTC-02:00" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC-02:00">UTC-02:00</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Postcodes_in_the_United_Kingdom#British_Overseas_Territories" title="Postcodes in the United Kingdom">UK postcode</a></th><td class="adr"><div class="postal-code">SIQQ 1xx</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Date format</th><td>dd/mm/yyyy</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Left-_and_right-hand_traffic" title="Left- and right-hand traffic">Driving side</a></th><td>left</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="Telephone numbers in South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">Calling code</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="Telephone numbers in South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">+500</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:GS" title="ISO 3166-2:GS">GS</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.gs" title=".gs">.gs</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands</b> (SGSSI) is a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territory</a> in the southern <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>. It is a remote and inhospitable collection of islands, consisting of <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_Island" title="South Georgia Island">South Georgia</a> and a chain of smaller islands known as the South Sandwich Islands. South Georgia is 165 kilometres (103&#160;mi) long and 35 kilometres (22&#160;mi) wide and is by far the largest island in the territory. The South Sandwich Islands lie about 700 kilometres (430&#160;mi) southeast of South Georgia. The territory's total land area is 3,903&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (1,507&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> are about 1,300 kilometres (810&#160;mi) west-northwest from its nearest point.
</p><p>No permanent native population lives in the South Sandwich Islands, and a very small non-permanent population resides on South Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-population_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-population-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> There are no scheduled passenger flights or ferries to or from the territory, although visits by cruise liners to South Georgia are increasingly popular, with several thousand visitors each summer.
</p><p>The United Kingdom claimed <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> over South Georgia in 1775 and the South Sandwich Islands in 1908. The territory of "South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands" was formed in 1985; previously, it had been governed as part of the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands_Dependencies" title="Falkland Islands Dependencies">Falkland Islands Dependencies</a>. <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> claimed South Georgia in 1927 and claimed the South Sandwich Islands in 1938.
</p><p>Argentina maintained a naval station, <a href="/wiki/Corbeta_Uruguay" class="mw-redirect" title="Corbeta Uruguay">Corbeta Uruguay</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Thule_Island" title="Thule Island">Thule Island</a> in the South Sandwich Islands from 1976 until 1982 when it was closed by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>. The Argentine claim over South Georgia contributed to the 1982 <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a>, during which Argentine forces briefly occupied the island. Argentina <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_and_South_Sandwich_Islands_sovereignty_dispute" class="mw-redirect" title="South Georgia and South Sandwich Islands sovereignty dispute">continues to claim sovereignty</a> over South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Dissostichus" title="Dissostichus">Toothfish</a> are vital to the islands' economy; as a result, Toothfish Day is celebrated on 4 September as a <a href="/wiki/Bank_holiday" title="Bank holiday">bank holiday</a> in the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="History of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">History of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Georgia">South Georgia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: South Georgia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="17th.E2.80.9319th_centuries"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="17th–19th_centuries">17th–19th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 17th–19th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Island of South Georgia is said to have been first sighted in 1675 by <a href="/wiki/Anthony_de_la_Roch%C3%A9" title="Anthony de la Roché">Anthony de la Roché</a>, a London merchant,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and was named <i>Roche Island</i> on a number of early maps.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It was sighted by the commercial Spanish ship <i>León</i> operating out of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Malo" title="Saint-Malo">Saint-Malo</a> on 28 June or 29 June 1756.<sup id="cite_ref-Iberoamerica_–_Bienvenido_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iberoamerica_–_Bienvenido-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> At one time it was confused with <a href="/wiki/Pepys_Island" title="Pepys Island">Pepys Island</a>, which was "discovered" by <a href="/wiki/William_Dampier" title="William Dampier">William Dampier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ambrose_Cowley" title="Ambrose Cowley">Ambrose Cowley</a> in 1683 but later proved to be a <a href="/wiki/Phantom_island" title="Phantom island">phantom island</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> circumnavigated the island in 1775 and made the first landing. He claimed the territory for the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a>, and named it the Isle of Georgia, in honour of King <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George III of the United Kingdom">George III</a>. British arrangements for the government of South Georgia were established under the 1843 British <a href="/wiki/Letters_Patent" class="mw-redirect" title="Letters Patent">Letters Patent</a>.
</p><p>In 1882–1883, a German expedition for the first <a href="/wiki/International_Polar_Year" title="International Polar Year">International Polar Year</a> was stationed at <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bay" title="Royal Bay">Royal Bay</a> on the southeast side of the island. The scientists of this group observed the <a href="/wiki/Transit_of_Venus" title="Transit of Venus">transit of Venus</a> and recorded waves produced by the <a href="/wiki/1883_eruption_of_Krakatoa" title="1883 eruption of Krakatoa">1883 eruption of Krakatoa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Seal_hunting" title="Seal hunting">Seal hunting</a> at South Georgia began in 1786 and continued throughout the 19th century. The waters proved treacherous and a number of vessels were wrecked there, such as <a href="/wiki/Earl_Spencer_(1799_ship)" title="Earl Spencer (1799 ship)"><i>Earl Spencer</i></a>, in late-1801.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_and_21st_centuries">20th and 21st centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 20th and 21st centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grytviken_church.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Grytviken_church.jpg/220px-Grytviken_church.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Grytviken_church.jpg/330px-Grytviken_church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Grytviken_church.jpg/440px-Grytviken_church.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grytviken_church.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Lutheran_Church_(Grytviken,_South_Georgia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian Lutheran Church (Grytviken, South Georgia)">Norwegian Lutheran Church at Grytviken</a></div></div></div>
<p>South Georgia became a base for <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a> beginning in the 20th century, until whaling ended in the 1960s. A Norwegian, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Anton_Larsen" title="Carl Anton Larsen">Carl Anton Larsen</a>, established the first land-based whaling station and first permanent habitation at <a href="/wiki/Grytviken" title="Grytviken">Grytviken</a> in 1904. It operated through his <a href="/wiki/Compa%C3%B1%C3%ADa_Argentina_de_Pesca" title="Compañía Argentina de Pesca">Argentine Fishing Company</a>, which settled in Grytviken.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Iberoamerica_–_Bienvenido_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iberoamerica_–_Bienvenido-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The station operated until 1965. Whaling stations operated under leases granted by the Governor of the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>. The seven stations, all on the north coast with its sheltered harbours, were, from the west to east:
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Prince_Olav_Harbour" title="Prince Olav Harbour">Prince Olav Harbour</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leith_Harbour" title="Leith Harbour">Leith Harbour</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stromness_(South_Georgia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stromness (South Georgia)">Stromness</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Husvik" title="Husvik">Husvik</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grytviken" title="Grytviken">Grytviken</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Godthul" title="Godthul">Godthul</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ocean_Harbour" title="Ocean Harbour">Ocean Harbour</a></li></ol>
</div>
<p>The whaling stations' <a href="/wiki/Trywork" title="Trywork">tryworks</a> were unpleasant and dangerous places to work. One was called "a <a href="/wiki/Charnel_house" title="Charnel house">charnel house</a> boiling wholesale in Vaseline" by an early 20th-century visitor. <a href="/wiki/Tim_Flannery" title="Tim Flannery">Tim Flannery</a> wrote that its "putrid vapors [resembled] the pong of bad fish, manure, and a tanning works mixed together", and noted one bizarre peril: "A rotting whale could fill with gas to bursting, ejecting a fetus the size of a motor vehicle with sufficient force to kill a man."<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PanoramaOfSouthGeorgia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/PanoramaOfSouthGeorgia.jpg/220px-PanoramaOfSouthGeorgia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="84" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/PanoramaOfSouthGeorgia.jpg/330px-PanoramaOfSouthGeorgia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/PanoramaOfSouthGeorgia.jpg/440px-PanoramaOfSouthGeorgia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="792" data-file-height="303" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PanoramaOfSouthGeorgia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>South Georgia, photographed by <a href="/wiki/Frank_Hurley" title="Frank Hurley">Frank Hurley</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Trans-Antarctic_Expedition" title="Imperial Trans-Antarctic Expedition">Imperial Trans-Antarctic Expedition</a></div></div></div>
<p>With the end of the whaling industry, the stations were abandoned. Apart from a few preserved buildings such as the <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_Museum" title="South Georgia Museum">South Georgia Museum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Lutheran_Church_(Grytviken,_South_Georgia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian Lutheran Church (Grytviken, South Georgia)">Norwegian Lutheran Church at Grytviken</a>, only their decaying remains survive. From 1905, the Argentine Meteorological Office cooperated in maintaining a meteorological observatory at Grytviken under the British lease requirements of the whaling station until these changed in 1949.
</p><p>In 1908, the United Kingdom issued further <a href="/wiki/Letters_patent" title="Letters patent">letters patent</a> that established constitutional arrangements for its possessions in the South Atlantic. The letters covered South Georgia, the <a href="/wiki/South_Orkneys" class="mw-redirect" title="South Orkneys">South Orkneys</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_Shetlands" class="mw-redirect" title="South Shetlands">South Shetlands</a>, the South Sandwich Islands, and <a href="/wiki/Graham_Land" title="Graham Land">Graham Land</a>. The claim was extended in 1917 to include a sector of Antarctica reaching to the <a href="/wiki/South_Pole" title="South Pole">South Pole</a>. In 1909, an administrative centre and residence were established at King Edward Point on South Georgia, near the whaling station of Grytviken. A permanent local British administration and resident magistrate exercised effective <a href="/wiki/Possession_(law)" title="Possession (law)">possession</a>, enforcement of <a href="/wiki/British_law" class="mw-redirect" title="British law">British law</a>, and regulation of all economic, scientific, and other activities in the territory, which was then governed as the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands_Dependencies" title="Falkland Islands Dependencies">Falkland Islands Dependencies</a>. In about 1912, what is according to some accounts the largest whale ever caught, a <a href="/wiki/Blue_whale" title="Blue whale">blue whale</a> of 110 feet (34&#160;m), was landed at Grytviken.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 1916, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Shackleton" title="Ernest Shackleton">Ernest Shackleton</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Trans-Antarctic_Expedition" title="Imperial Trans-Antarctic Expedition">Imperial Trans-Antarctic Expedition</a> became stranded on <a href="/wiki/Elephant_Island" title="Elephant Island">Elephant Island</a>, some 800 miles (1,300&#160;km) southwest of South Georgia. Shackleton and five companions set out in a small boat to summon help, and on 10 May, after an epic voyage, they landed at <a href="/wiki/King_Haakon_Bay" title="King Haakon Bay">King Haakon Bay</a> on South Georgia's south coast. While three stayed at the coast, Shackleton and the two others, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Crean_(explorer)" title="Tom Crean (explorer)">Tom Crean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Worsley" title="Frank Worsley">Frank Worsley</a>, went on to cover 22 miles (35&#160;km) over the spine of the mountainous island to reach help at <a href="/wiki/Stromness,_South_Georgia" title="Stromness, South Georgia">Stromness</a> whaling station. The remaining 22 members of the expedition, who had stayed on Elephant Island, were subsequently rescued. In January 1922, during a <a href="/wiki/Shackleton%E2%80%93Rowett_Expedition" title="Shackleton–Rowett Expedition">later expedition</a>, Shackleton died on board ship while moored in King Edward Cove, South Georgia. He is buried at Grytviken. The ashes of another noted Antarctic explorer, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Wild" title="Frank Wild">Frank Wild</a>, who had been Shackleton's second-in-command on the Imperial Trans-Antarctic Expedition, were interred next to Shackleton in 2011.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SG-Settlements.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/SG-Settlements.png/220px-SG-Settlements.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/SG-Settlements.png/330px-SG-Settlements.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/SG-Settlements.png/440px-SG-Settlements.png 2x" data-file-width="3702" data-file-height="2684" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SG-Settlements.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Historical and modern settlements of South Georgia Island</div></div></div>
<p>Argentina claimed South Georgia in 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, the Royal Navy deployed an armed merchant vessel to patrol South Georgian and Antarctic waters against German raiders, along with two four-inch shore guns (still present) protecting Cumberland Bay and Stromness Bay, which were manned by volunteers from among the Norwegian whalers. The base at King Edward Point was expanded as a research facility in 1949/1950 by the <a href="/wiki/British_Antarctic_Survey" title="British Antarctic Survey">British Antarctic Survey</a>, which until 1962 was called the Falkland Islands Dependencies Survey.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a> was precipitated on 19 March 1982 when a group of Argentinians (most of them <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Marines" class="mw-redirect" title="Argentine Marines">Argentine Marines</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mufti_(dress)" title="Mufti (dress)"><i>mufti</i></a>), posing as scrap-metal merchants, occupied the abandoned whaling station at <a href="/wiki/Leith_Harbour" title="Leith Harbour">Leith Harbour</a> on South Georgia. On 3 April, the Argentine troops <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grytviken" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Grytviken">attacked and occupied Grytviken</a>. Among the commanding officers of the Argentine garrison was <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Astiz" title="Alfredo Astiz">Alfredo Astiz</a>, a captain in the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Navy" title="Argentine Navy">Argentine Navy</a> who was convicted years later of crimes against humanity committed during the <a href="/wiki/Dirty_War" title="Dirty War">Dirty War</a> in Argentina.
</p><p>The island was recaptured by British forces on 25 April, in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Paraquet" title="Operation Paraquet">Operation Paraquet</a>. In 1985, South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands ceased to be administered as a Falkland Islands Dependency and became a separate territory. The <a href="/wiki/King_Edward_Point" title="King Edward Point">King Edward Point</a> base, which had become a small military garrison after the Falklands War, returned to civilian use in 2001 and is now operated by the <a href="/wiki/British_Antarctic_Survey" title="British Antarctic Survey">British Antarctic Survey</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Sandwich_Islands">South Sandwich Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: South Sandwich Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> discovered the southern eight islands of the Sandwich Islands Group in 1775, although he lumped the southernmost three together, and their status as separate islands was not established until 1820 by <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Gottlieb_von_Bellingshausen" title="Fabian Gottlieb von Bellingshausen">Fabian Gottlieb von Bellingshausen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The northern three islands were discovered by Bellingshausen in 1819. The islands were tentatively named "Sandwich Land" by Cook, although he also commented that they might be a group of islands rather than a single body of land. The name was chosen in honour of <a href="/wiki/John_Montagu,_4th_Earl_of_Sandwich" title="John Montagu, 4th Earl of Sandwich">John Montagu, 4th Earl of Sandwich</a>, First Lord of the Admiralty. The word "South" was later added to distinguish them from the "Sandwich Islands", now known as the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands" title="Hawaiian Islands">Hawaiian Islands</a>.
</p><p>Argentina claimed the South Sandwich Islands in 1938, and challenged British sovereignty in the Islands on several occasions. From 25 January 1955 to mid-1956, Argentina maintained the summer station Teniente Esquivel at <a href="/wiki/Ferguson_Bay" title="Ferguson Bay">Ferguson Bay</a> on the southeastern coast of <a href="/wiki/Thule_Island" title="Thule Island">Thule Island</a>. Argentina maintained a naval base (<a href="/wiki/Corbeta_Uruguay" class="mw-redirect" title="Corbeta Uruguay">Corbeta Uruguay</a>) from 1976 to 1982, in the lee (southern east coast) of the same island. Although the British discovered the presence of the Argentine base in 1976,<sup id="cite_ref-Freedman2005_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedman2005-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> protested and tried to resolve the issue by diplomatic means, no effort was made to remove them by force until after the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a>. The base was removed on 20 June 1982.
</p><p>On 10 February 2008, a 6.5 magnitude <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">earthquake</a> had its epicentre 205&#160;km (127&#160;mi; 111&#160;nmi) south-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Island" title="Bristol Island">Bristol Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> On 30 June 2008 at 06:17:53 UTC, a 7.0-magnitude earthquake struck the region. Its epicentre was at 58.160S 21.893W, 283&#160;km (176&#160;mi; 153&#160;nmi) ENE (73 degrees) of Bristol Island.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The United States Geological Survey reported that a 7.3-magnitude earthquake had occurred at 10:04 EDT on 15 Jul 2013, 216&#160;km (134&#160;mi; 117&#160;nmi) south-southeast of Bristol Island, South Sandwich Islands, at a depth of 31.3&#160;km (19.4&#160;mi). The epicentre was located 2,230&#160;km (1,390&#160;mi; 1,200&#160;nmi) southeast of <a href="/wiki/Stanley,_Falkland_Islands" title="Stanley, Falkland Islands">Stanley, Falkland Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Georgia_and_South_Sandwich_Islands.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/South_Georgia_and_South_Sandwich_Islands.png/220px-South_Georgia_and_South_Sandwich_Islands.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/South_Georgia_and_South_Sandwich_Islands.png/330px-South_Georgia_and_South_Sandwich_Islands.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/18/South_Georgia_and_South_Sandwich_Islands.png 2x" data-file-width="337" data-file-height="360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Georgia_and_South_Sandwich_Islands.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>CIA map of the islands</div></div></div>
<p>South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands are a collection of islands in the South Atlantic Ocean. Most of the islands, rising steeply from the sea, are rugged and mountainous. At higher elevations, the islands are permanently covered with ice and snow.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Georgia_group">South Georgia group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: South Georgia group">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The South Georgia group lies about 1,390 kilometres (860&#160;mi; 750&#160;nmi) east-southeast of the Falkland Islands, at 54°–55°S, 36°–38°W. It comprises <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_Island" title="South Georgia Island">South Georgia Island</a> itself—by far the largest island in the territory—, and the islands that immediately surround it and some remote and isolated islets to the west and east-southeast. It has a total land area of 3,756 square kilometres (1,450&#160;sq&#160;mi), including satellite islands, but excluding the South Sandwich Islands which form a separate island group.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islands_within_the_South_Georgia_group">Islands within the South Georgia group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Islands within the South Georgia group">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1989_Grytvikken_hg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/1989_Grytvikken_hg.jpg/220px-1989_Grytvikken_hg.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/1989_Grytvikken_hg.jpg/330px-1989_Grytvikken_hg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/1989_Grytvikken_hg.jpg/440px-1989_Grytvikken_hg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2439" data-file-height="1527" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1989_Grytvikken_hg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Grytviken" title="Grytviken">Grytviken</a></div></div></div>
<p>South Georgia Island lies at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;params=54_15_S_36_45_W_scale:2500000"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">54°15′S</span> <span class="longitude">36°45′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">54.250°S 36.750°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">-54.250; -36.750</span></span></span></a></span><span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;params=54_15_S_36_45_W_scale:2500000"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">54°15′S</span> <span class="longitude">36°45′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">54.250°S 36.750°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">-54.250; -36.750</span></span></span></a></span></span></span> and has an area of 3,528 square kilometres (1,362&#160;sq&#160;mi). It is mountainous and largely barren. Eleven peaks rise to over 2,000 metres (6,600&#160;ft) high, their slopes furrowed with deep gorges filled with glaciers; the largest is <a href="/wiki/Fortuna_Glacier" title="Fortuna Glacier">Fortuna Glacier</a>. The highest peak is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Paget" title="Mount Paget">Mount Paget</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Allardyce_Range" title="Allardyce Range">Allardyce Range</a> at 2,934 metres (9,626&#160;ft).
</p><p>Geologically, the island consists of <a href="/wiki/Gneiss" title="Gneiss">gneiss</a> and <a href="/wiki/Argillaceous_schist" title="Argillaceous schist">argillaceous schists</a> with occasional tufts and other sedimentary layers from which fossils have been recovered.<sup id="cite_ref-trendall_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trendall-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The island is a fragment of some greater land-mass now vanished and was probably a former extension of the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andean system</a>.
</p><p>Smaller islands and islets off the coast of South Georgia Island include:
</p>
<div>

<p>These remote rocks are also considered part of the South Georgia group:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Shag_Rocks_(South_Georgia)" title="Shag Rocks (South Georgia)">Shag Rocks</a>, 185&#160;km (115&#160;mi; 100&#160;nmi) west-northwest of South Georgia Island</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Black_Rock_(South_Georgia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Rock (South Georgia)">Black Rock</a>, 169&#160;km (105&#160;mi; 91&#160;nmi) west-northwest of South Georgia Island</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clerke_Rocks" title="Clerke Rocks">Clerke Rocks</a>, 56&#160;km (35&#160;mi; 30&#160;nmi) east-southeast of South Georgia Island</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Sandwich_Islands_2">South Sandwich Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: South Sandwich Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montagu_Island_Satellite_Photograph.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Montagu_Island_Satellite_Photograph.jpg/220px-Montagu_Island_Satellite_Photograph.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Montagu_Island_Satellite_Photograph.jpg/330px-Montagu_Island_Satellite_Photograph.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Montagu_Island_Satellite_Photograph.jpg/440px-Montagu_Island_Satellite_Photograph.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="460" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montagu_Island_Satellite_Photograph.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NASA satellite photograph of Montagu Island</div></div></div>
<p>The South Sandwich Islands (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Islas Sandwich del Sur</i>) comprise 11 mostly <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanic</a> islands (excluding tiny satellite islands and offshore rocks), with some active volcanoes. They form an <a href="/wiki/Island_arc" title="Island arc">island arc</a> running north-south in the region 56°18'–59°27'S, 26°23'–28°08'W, between about 350 and 500&#160;mi (300 and 430&#160;nmi; 560 and 800&#160;km) southeast of South Georgia.
</p><p>The northernmost of the South Sandwich Islands form the <a href="/wiki/Traversay_Islands" title="Traversay Islands">Traversay Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Candlemas_Islands" title="Candlemas Islands">Candlemas Islands</a> groups, while the southernmost make up <a href="/wiki/Southern_Thule" title="Southern Thule">Southern Thule</a>. The three largest islands&#160;&#8211;&#32;<a href="/wiki/Saunders_Island,_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="Saunders Island, South Sandwich Islands">Saunders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montagu_Island" title="Montagu Island">Montagu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Island" title="Bristol Island">Bristol</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32;lie between the two. The Islands' highest point is Mount Belinda (1,370&#160;m or 4,495&#160;ft) on Montagu Island.
</p><p>The South Sandwich Islands are uninhabited, though a permanently manned Argentine research station was located on Thule Island from 1976 to 1982 (for details, see <a href="#History"> §&#160;History</a> above). Automatic <a href="/wiki/Weather_station" title="Weather station">weather stations</a> are on Thule Island and <a href="/wiki/Zavodovski_Island" title="Zavodovski Island">Zavodovski</a>. To the northwest of Zavodovski Island is the <a href="/wiki/Protector_Shoal" title="Protector Shoal">Protector Shoal</a>, a submarine volcano.
</p>
<table class="noprint infobox" id="GeoGroup" style="width: 23em; font-size: 88%; line-height: 1.5em">

<td align="right">310&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (120&#160;sq&#160;mi)</td>

<p>A series of six passages separates each of the islands or island groups in the chain. They are, from north to south: Zavodovski Isl.&#160;&#8211;&#32;<i>Traverse passage</i>&#160;&#8211;&#32;Visokoi Isl.&#160;&#8211;&#32;<i>Brown's passage</i>&#160;&#8211;&#32;Candlemas Isl.&#160;&#8211;&#32;<i>Shackleton's passage</i>&#160;&#8211;&#32;Saunders Isl.&#160;&#8211;&#32;<i>Larsen's passage</i>&#160;&#8211;&#32;Montagu Isl.&#160;&#8211;&#32;<i>Biscoe's passage</i>&#160;&#8211;&#32;Bristol Isl.&#160;&#8211;&#32;<a href="/wiki/Forsters_Passage" title="Forsters Passage">Forsters Passage</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32;Southern Thule. Nelson Channel is the passage between Candlemas and Vindication Island.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extreme_points">Extreme points</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Extreme points">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Northernmost point – <a href="/wiki/Cape_North_(South_Georgia)" title="Cape North (South Georgia)">Cape North</a></li>
<li>Southernmost point – on <a href="/wiki/Cook_Island,_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="Cook Island, South Sandwich Islands">Cook Island</a></li>
<li>Westernmost point – on <a href="/wiki/Main_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Main Island">Main Island</a> (of the <a href="/wiki/Willis_Islands" title="Willis Islands">Willis Islands</a>)</li>
<li>Easternmost point – on <a href="/wiki/Montagu_Island" title="Montagu Island">Montagu Island</a></li>
<li>Highest point – <a href="/wiki/Mount_Paget" title="Mount Paget">Mount Paget</a>: 2,934 m</li>
<li>Lowest point – Atlantic Ocean: 0</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SouthGeorgiaIsland-EO.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/SouthGeorgiaIsland-EO.JPG/220px-SouthGeorgiaIsland-EO.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/SouthGeorgiaIsland-EO.JPG/330px-SouthGeorgiaIsland-EO.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/SouthGeorgiaIsland-EO.JPG/440px-SouthGeorgiaIsland-EO.JPG 2x" data-file-width="876" data-file-height="606" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SouthGeorgiaIsland-EO.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NASA satellite image of South Georgia Island covered with snow</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wave_Clouds_from_South_Sandwich_Islands.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Wave_Clouds_from_South_Sandwich_Islands.jpg/220px-Wave_Clouds_from_South_Sandwich_Islands.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="286" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Wave_Clouds_from_South_Sandwich_Islands.jpg/330px-Wave_Clouds_from_South_Sandwich_Islands.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Wave_Clouds_from_South_Sandwich_Islands.jpg/440px-Wave_Clouds_from_South_Sandwich_Islands.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wave_Clouds_from_South_Sandwich_Islands.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The South Sandwich Islands connect with air currents to make <a href="/wiki/Wave_cloud" title="Wave cloud">wave patterns</a> in clouds.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Bay_and_South_Georgia_Island.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Royal_Bay_and_South_Georgia_Island.jpg/220px-Royal_Bay_and_South_Georgia_Island.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Royal_Bay_and_South_Georgia_Island.jpg/330px-Royal_Bay_and_South_Georgia_Island.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Royal_Bay_and_South_Georgia_Island.jpg/440px-Royal_Bay_and_South_Georgia_Island.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Bay_and_South_Georgia_Island.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Royal Bay and South Georgia Island</div></div></div>
<p>The climate is classified as polar, and the weather is highly variable and harsh; making a <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a> (ET) in Köppen climate classification. Typical daily maximum temperatures in South Georgia at sea level are around 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) in winter (August) and 8&#160;°C (46.4&#160;°F) in summer (January). Winter minimum temperatures are typically about −5&#160;°C (23&#160;°F) and rarely dip below −10&#160;°C (14&#160;°F). Annual precipitation in South Georgia is about 1,500&#160;mm (59.1&#160;in), much of which falls as sleet or snow, which is possible the entire year. Inland, the snow line in summer is at an altitude of about 300&#160;m (984&#160;ft).
</p><p>Westerly winds blow throughout the year interspersed with periods of calm—indeed, in 1963, 25% of winds were in the calm category at King Edward point, and the mean wind speed of around 8 knots (9.2&#160;mph; 15&#160;km/h) is around half that of the Falkland Islands. This gives the eastern side of South Georgia (leeward side) a more pleasant climate than the exposed western side. The prevailing weather conditions generally make the islands difficult to approach by ship, though the north coast of South Georgia has several large bays which provide good anchorage.
</p><p>Sunshine, as with many South Atlantic Islands, is low, at a maximum of just 21.5%. This amounts to around 1,000 hours of sunshine annually. The local <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topography</a>, however, also contributes significantly to the low <a href="/wiki/Insolation" class="mw-redirect" title="Insolation">insolation</a>. A study published during the early 1960s<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> indicated that sunshine recording instruments remained significantly obscured throughout the year and entirely obscured during June. It was estimated that the theoretical sunshine exposure minus obstructions would be around 14% at Bird Island and 35% at King Edward Point&#160;&#8211;&#32;or, in hourly terms, ranging from around 650 hours in the west to 1,500 hours in the east. This illustrates the effect the Allardyce range has in breaking up cloud cover.
</p><p>Mountain winds blow straight up the western side and straight down the eastern side of the mountains and become much warmer and drier due to the <a href="/wiki/Foehn_wind" title="Foehn wind">Föhn effect</a>; this produces the most pleasant conditions when temperatures can occasionally rise over 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F) on summer days. The highest recorded temperature was 28.8&#160;°C (83.8&#160;°F) at Grytviken.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and 26.3&#160;°C (79.3&#160;°F) at nearby King Edward point, both on the sheltered east side of the Islands. Conversely, the highest recorded temperature at Bird Island on the windward western side is a mere 14.5&#160;°C (58.1&#160;°F). As one might expect, the sheltered eastern side can also record lower winter temperatures—the absolute minimum for Grytviken being −19.4&#160;°C (−2.9&#160;°F), King Edward Point −18.9&#160;°C (−2.0&#160;°F), but Bird Island just −11.4&#160;°C (11.5&#160;°F).
</p><p>The seas surrounding South Georgia are cold throughout the year due to the proximity of the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Circumpolar_Current" title="Antarctic Circumpolar Current">Antarctic Circumpolar Current</a>. They usually remain free of pack ice in winter, though thin ice may form in sheltered bays, and <a href="/wiki/Iceberg" title="Iceberg">icebergs</a> are common.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Sea temperatures drop to 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) in late August and rise to around 4&#160;°C (39.2&#160;°F) only in early April.
</p><p>The South Sandwich Islands are much colder than South Georgia, being farther south and more exposed to cold outbreaks from the Antarctic continent. They are also surrounded by sea ice from the middle of May to late November (even longer at their southern end).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Recorded temperature extremes at South Thule Island have ranged from −29.8 to 17.7&#160;°C (−21.6 to 63.9&#160;°F).
</p>

<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left">Research Stations</div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center;text-align:left;padding-top:0;"><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><b><a href="/wiki/British_Antarctic_Survey" title="British Antarctic Survey">British Antarctic Survey</a></b></div>
<hr />
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/King_Edward_Point" title="King Edward Point">King Edward Point</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bird_Island,_South_Georgia" title="Bird Island, South Georgia">Bird Island</a></li></ul></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">
<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left">Other</div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center;text-align:left;padding-top:0;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Flag_of_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="Flag of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">Flag</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="Languages of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">Languages</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Postage_stamps_and_postal_history_of_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="Postage stamps and postal history of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">Postal History</a></li></ul></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">
<div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_political_science#Politics_by_region" title="Outline of political science">Other countries</a></li>
<li><a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Atlas_of_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" class="extiw" title="commons:Atlas of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">Atlas</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="Template:Politics of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Politics_of_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Template talk:Politics of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands (page does not exist)"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Executive power is vested in the <a href="/wiki/Monarch_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Monarch of the United Kingdom">Monarch of the United Kingdom</a> and is exercised by the <a href="/wiki/Commissioner_for_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="Commissioner for South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">commissioner</a>, a post held by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_Falkland_Islands" title="Governor of the Falkland Islands">Governor of the Falkland Islands</a>. The current commissioner is <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Phillips" title="Nigel Phillips">Nigel Phillips</a>, who became commissioner on 12 September 2017. A chief executive officer (Martin Collins) deals with policy matters and is director of SGSSI Fisheries, responsible for the allocation of fishing licences. An executive officer (Richard McKee) deals with administrative matters relating to the territory. Also, an environmental officer (Jennifer Lee) and a marine and Fisheries officer (Katherine Ross) are appointed. The financial secretary and attorney general of the territory are appointed <i>ex officio</i> similar appointments in the Falkland Islands' government.
</p><p>As no permanent inhabitants live on the islands, no <a href="/wiki/Legislative_council" title="Legislative council">legislative council</a> and no elections are needed. The UK Foreign Office manages the foreign relations of the territory. Since 1982, the territory celebrates <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Day" title="Liberation Day">Liberation Day</a> on 14 June.
</p><p>The constitution of the territory (adopted 3 October 1985), the manner in which its government is directed and the availability of judicial review were discussed in a series of litigations between 2001 and 2005 (see, in particular, <i>Regina v. Secretary of State for Foreign and Commonwealth Affairs (Appellant) ex parte Quark Fishing Limited</i> [2005] UKHL 57<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>). Although its government is entirely directed by the UK Foreign Office, it was held that, since it was acting as an agent of <a href="/wiki/The_Crown#Divisiblity_of_the_Crown" title="The Crown">the Crown</a> in right of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands rather than in right of the UK, its decisions under that direction could not be challenged as if they were in law decisions of a UK government department;<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> thus the European Convention on Human Rights did not apply.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Commercial <a href="/wiki/Seal_hunting" title="Seal hunting">sealing</a> occurred on the islands between 1817 and 1909. During that period twenty visits are recorded by sealing vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Economic activity in South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands is limited. The territory has revenues of £4.5&#160;million, 80% of which is derived from fishing licences (2011 figures).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Other sources of revenue are the sale of postage stamps and coins, tourism, and customs and harbour dues.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fishing">Fishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Fishing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Fishing takes place around South Georgia and in adjacent waters in some months of the year, with fishing licences sold by the territory for <a href="/wiki/Patagonian_toothfish" title="Patagonian toothfish">Patagonian toothfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nototheniidae" title="Nototheniidae">cod icefish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Krill" title="Krill">krill</a>. Fishing licences bring in millions of pounds a year, most of which is spent on fishery protection and research. All fisheries are regulated and managed in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Convention_for_the_Conservation_of_Antarctic_Marine_Living_Resources" title="Convention for the Conservation of Antarctic Marine Living Resources">Convention for the Conservation of Antarctic Marine Living Resources</a> (CCAMLR) system.
</p><p>In 2001 the South Georgia government was cited by the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Stewardship_Council" title="Marine Stewardship Council">Marine Stewardship Council</a> for its sustainable Patagonian toothfish fishery, certifying that South Georgia met the MSC's environmental standards. The certificate places limits on the timing and quantity of Patagonian toothfish that may be caught.<sup id="cite_ref-Whole_Foods_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whole_Foods-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">Tourism</a> has become a larger source of income in recent years, with many cruise ships and sailing yachts visiting the area (the only way to visit South Georgia is by sea; there are no airstrips on the Islands). The territory gains income from landing charges and the sale of souvenirs. <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">Cruise ships</a> often combine a Grytviken visit with a trip to the Antarctic Peninsula.
</p><p>Charter yacht visits usually begin in the Falkland Islands, last between four and six weeks, and enable guests to visit remote harbours of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands. Sailing vessels are now required to anchor out and can no longer tie up to the old whaling piers on shore. One exception to this is the recently upgraded/repaired yacht berth at Grytviken. All other jetties at former whaling stations lie inside a 200&#160;m (656&#160;ft) exclusion zone; and berthing, or putting ropes ashore, at these is forbidden. Yachts visiting South Georgia are normally expected to report to the Government Officers at King Edward Point before moving round the island.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Postage_stamps">Postage stamps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Postage stamps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Postage_stamps_and_postal_history_of_South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="Postage stamps and postal history of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">Postage stamps and postal history of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands</a></div>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2010</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stamp_South_Georgia_1963_4d.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Stamp_South_Georgia_1963_4d.jpg/220px-Stamp_South_Georgia_1963_4d.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Stamp_South_Georgia_1963_4d.jpg/330px-Stamp_South_Georgia_1963_4d.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/c3/Stamp_South_Georgia_1963_4d.jpg 2x" data-file-width="403" data-file-height="248" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stamp_South_Georgia_1963_4d.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This postage stamp depicting a <a href="/wiki/Fin_whale" title="Fin whale">fin whale</a> was issued in 1963.</div></div></div>
<p>A large source of income from abroad also comes from the issue of South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands postage stamps which are produced in the UK.
</p><p>A reasonable issue policy (few sets of stamps are issued each year) along with attractive subject matter (especially whales) makes them popular with <a href="/wiki/Topical_stamp_collecting" title="Topical stamp collecting">topical stamp collectors</a>.
</p><p>There are only four genuine <a href="/wiki/First_day_cover" class="mw-redirect" title="First day cover">first day cover</a> sets from 16 March 1982 in existence. They were stamped at the South Georgia Post Office; all those in circulation were stamped elsewhere and sent out, but the only genuine ones were kept at the Post Office on South Georgia. These four sets were removed during the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a> by a member of staff of the British Antarctic Survey in the few moments the Argentinians allowed them to gather their belongings. Everything else was burnt, but these four sets were saved and brought to the UK by Robert Headland, BAS.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Currency">Currency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Currency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling_in_the_South_Atlantic_and_the_Antarctic" title="Pound sterling in the South Atlantic and the Antarctic">Pound sterling in the South Atlantic and the Antarctic</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">pound sterling</a> is the official currency of the islands, and the same notes and coins are used as in the United Kingdom.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet_domain_registration">Internet domain registration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Internet domain registration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> <a href="/wiki/Country_code" title="Country code">country code</a> <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">top-level domain</a> (<a href="/wiki/CcTLD" class="mw-redirect" title="CcTLD">ccTLD</a>) for South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands is <a href="/wiki/.gs" title=".gs">.gs</a>.  Although the territory has no permanent residents, the domain suffix has some popularity for website registrations, with approximately 6 million instances as of November 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<center>
<table>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plants">Plants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Plants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The parts of the islands that are not permanently covered in snow or ice are part of the <a href="/wiki/Scotia_Sea" title="Scotia Sea">Scotia Sea</a> Islands <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a>. In total there are 26 species of vascular plant native to South Georgia; six species of <a href="/wiki/Poaceae" title="Poaceae">grass</a>, four <a href="/wiki/Juncaceae" title="Juncaceae">rushes</a>, a single <a href="/wiki/Cyperaceae" title="Cyperaceae">sedge</a>, six <a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">ferns</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Lycopodiopsida" title="Lycopodiopsida">clubmoss</a> and nine small <a href="/wiki/Forb" title="Forb">forbs</a>. There are also about 125 species of <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">moss</a>, 85 of <a href="/wiki/Marchantiophyta" title="Marchantiophyta">liverworts</a> and 150 <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichens</a>, as well as about 50 species of macrofungi.<sup id="cite_ref-Headland_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Headland-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> A number of introduced species have become naturalised; many of these were introduced by whalers in cattle fodder, and some are considered invasive.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> There are no trees or shrubs on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The largest plant is the tussock grass <i><a href="/wiki/Poa_flabellata" title="Poa flabellata">Poa flabellata</a></i>. This grows mostly on raised beaches and steep slopes near the shore and may reach 2&#160;m (7&#160;ft). Other grasses include the tufted fescue (<i><a href="/wiki/Festuca_contracta" title="Festuca contracta">Festuca contracta</a></i>), the Alpine cat's-tail (<i><a href="/wiki/Phleum_alpinum" title="Phleum alpinum">Phleum alpinum</a></i>) and Antarctic hair-grass (<i><a href="/wiki/Deschampsia_antarctica" title="Deschampsia antarctica">Deschampsia antarctica</a></i>), and one of the commonest flowering plants is the greater burnet (<i><a href="/wiki/Acaena_magellanica" title="Acaena magellanica">Acaena magellanica</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Headland_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Headland-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Birds">Birds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Birds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>South Georgia supports many sea birds, including <a href="/wiki/Albatross" title="Albatross">albatross</a>, a large colony of <a href="/wiki/King_penguins" class="mw-redirect" title="King penguins">king penguins</a>, Macaroni penguins<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Penguin" title="Penguin">penguins</a> of various other species, along with <a href="/wiki/Petrel" title="Petrel">petrels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prion_(bird)" title="Prion (bird)">prions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shag_(bird)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shag (bird)">shags</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skua" title="Skua">skuas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gull" title="Gull">gulls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tern" title="Tern">terns</a>. Birds unique to the archipelago are the <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_shag" title="South Georgia shag">South Georgia shag</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_pipit" title="South Georgia pipit">South Georgia pipit</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_pintail" title="South Georgia pintail">South Georgia pintail</a>. Both South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands have been identified as <a href="/wiki/Important_Bird_Area" title="Important Bird Area">Important Bird Areas</a> (IBA) by <a href="/wiki/BirdLife_International" title="BirdLife International">BirdLife International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mammals">Mammals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Mammals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wikispecies-logo.svg/34px-Wikispecies-logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="34" height="40" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wikispecies-logo.svg/51px-Wikispecies-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wikispecies-logo.svg/68px-Wikispecies-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="941" data-file-height="1103" /></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist"><a href="/wiki/Wikispecies" title="Wikispecies">Wikispecies</a> has information related to <i><b><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:South_Georgia_Island_nonmarine_fauna" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Category:South Georgia Island nonmarine fauna">South Georgia Island nonmarine fauna</a></b></i></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">Seals</a> frequent the islands, and <a href="/wiki/Whale" title="Whale">whales</a> may be seen in the surrounding waters. There are no native land mammals, though <a href="/wiki/Reindeer" title="Reindeer">reindeer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brown_rat" title="Brown rat">brown rats</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_mouse" title="House mouse">mice</a> were introduced to South Georgia through human activities.
</p><p>Rats, brought to the island as stowaways on sealing and whaling ships in the late 18th century,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> have caused much damage to native wildlife, destroying tens of millions of ground-nesting birds' eggs and chicks. While previously the island's glaciers formed a natural barrier to the spread of rats, these glaciers are now slowly melting as the climate warms.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, scientists instituted a four-year programme to entirely eradicate the rats and mice, in what would be by far the largest rodent eradication attempt in the world to date.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The project was led by zoologist Anthony Martin of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Dundee" title="University of Dundee">The University of Dundee</a> who stated, "This is a man-induced problem and it's about time that man put right earlier errors."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In July 2013, the success of the main phase of the extermination of the rats, which took place in May that year, was announced. 180 tonnes of rat poison, <a href="/wiki/Brodifacoum" title="Brodifacoum">brodifacoum</a>, were dropped over 70% of the island, in what was the world's largest ever operation of this kind.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Another 95 tonnes of rat poison was planned to be dropped by three helicopters in January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In June 2015 the eradication programme concluded, apparently successfully, with the island believed "very likely" to be rat free. In 2017/18, an intensive six-month search by the South Georgia Heritage Trust, using sniffer dogs and baited traps, found no evidence of rodent presence.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Monitoring will continue for a further two or three years.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Reindeer_in_South_Georgia" title="Reindeer in South Georgia">Reindeer were introduced to South Georgia</a> in 1911 by Norwegian whalers for meat and for sport hunting. In February 2011, the authorities announced that due to the reindeer's detrimental effect on native species and the threat of their spreading to presently pristine areas, a complete cull would take place, leading to the eradication of reindeer from the island.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The eradication began in 2013 with 3,500 reindeer killed. Nearly all the rest were killed in early 2014, with the last (about 50) cleared in the 2014/15 southern summer.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_ecosystem">Marine ecosystem</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Marine ecosystem">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The seas around South Georgia have a high level of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>. In a recent study (2009–2011), South Georgia has been discovered to contain one of the highest levels of biodiversity among all the <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a> on Earth.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In respect to species, marine inhabitants endemic to this ecosystem outnumber and (in respect to biodiversity) surpass well-known regions such as the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos" class="mw-redirect" title="Galápagos">Galápagos</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The marine ecosystem is thought to be vulnerable because its low temperatures mean that it can repair itself only very slowly.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On 23 February 2012, to protect marine biodiversity, the territory's government created the South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands Marine Protected Area&#160;&#8211;&#32;comprising 1.07&#160;million&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (410,000&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<center>
<table>

<tbody><tr style="vertical-align:top;">
